asked the Minister of Irrigation and Water Management and Minister of Ports and Aviation : (a) Will he inform this House separately, the date on which the Villachchiya Tank and irrigation system that provided water to the Villachchiya Colony in the Anuradhapura District were reconstructed and the date on which the Colony was established? (b) Will he inform this House (i) the capacity of the relevant tank that provides water to the aforesaid colony, in acre feet; (ii) the extent of paddy lands cultivated by using that facility; and (iii) separately, the extent of land that has been cultivated under the Villachchiya Scheme during Yala and Maha seasons of the years 2005, 2006 and 2007? (c) Is he aware that the farm lands do not get sufficient water as a result of the poor irrigation system of this tank? (d) Will he submit to this House (i) whether action will be taken to repair the irrigation system of the tank; and (ii) if so, the date on which the aforesaid repair work will be started? (e) If not, why?

() , ? asked the Minister of Power and Energy : (a) Will he submit to this House (i) the number of State owned and private power stations that generate electricity and presently situated within Nuwara Eliya District and areas bordering it; (ii) the number of units of electricity produced annually by each of the aforesaid power stations; and (iii) the extent of land allocated for the reservoirs and other constructions and the number of families removed at the time of construction of each of the aforesaid power stations? (b) Will he state (i) separately, the number of grama niladhari divisions that have not been provided with electricity and the number of families that have not been provided with electricity supply within each Divisional Secretariat Division of Nuwara Eliya District; (ii) the number of Grama Niladhari divisions and the relevant number of families provided with electricity of low voltage, within the aforesaid Divisional Decretariat Divisions; and (iii) the measures taken to meet the needs of the aforesaid areas that have not been provided with electricity and with electricity of low voltage?

(c) Will he state (i) the number of electrification projects including the projects with Chinese aid, CIDA project and others that are to be implemented by the relevant Ministry; and (ii) out of the aforesaid number, the number of projects allocated for Nuwara Eliya District? (d) If not, why?

LEAVE OF ABSENCE : HON. P. ARIYANETHRAN

. ( . ) (The Hon. K. Thurairetnasingam)

, " . , 66() 2008 09 " . ( ) (The Hon. Kanagasabai Pathmanathan) . . Seconded.

, . . Question put, and agreed to. ( ) (Mr. Speaker) , .

: : PRIVILEGE: OBSTRUCTION IN PRAYING AT MADHU SHRINE ( ) (The Hon. (Dr.) Jayalath Jayawardana) , . 600 . 16 14 16 . 2007 3 . 16 . 2008 2008 2008 01, 2008 07 2008 12 . * . 2008 13 , .. , . 2008 14 7.30 . .

* . . Placed in the Library.

2008 09 85 86

" . ." . . , . , , , . , , 14 - - . 12(1), 12(2) 14(1)() , , , . 2008 27 * .

* : Document tabled IN THE HUMAN RIGHTS COMMISSIONS OF SRI LANKA Dr. Jayalath Jayawardana MBBS, FICS, MD Member of Parliament Democratic Socialist Republic of Sri Lanka 26B Samit Flats Jawatte Road Colombo 05 Vs (1) Mr. Gotabhaya Rajapakse Secretary, Ministry of Defence 15/5, Baladaksha Mawatha Colombo 3. (2) Colonel D. S. Weeraman Ministry of Defence Public Seccurity Law & Order Ministry of Defence 15/5, Baladaksha Mawatha Colombo 3. On this 27th day August 2008 To: The Honourable Chairman and the Honourable Commissioners of the Human Rights Commission of Sri Lanka. The complaint of the Complainant above named appearing by his Attorney-at-Law Priyalal Sirisena States as follows:- 1. The Complainant is a Citizen of Sri Lanka, a Medical Doctor, a Member of Parliament since 1994 and served as Minister of Rehabilitation, Resettlement and Refugees during the period 2002 to 2004.

2. The Complainant states that he and his family are staunch Roman Catholics. His piety has been recognised by the Roman Catholic Church and his Excellency The Apostolic Nuncia of Sri Lanka arranged for him and his family to be present at Midnight Christmas Mass in December 2006. Celebarated by His Holiness in Rome. 3. The Complainant states that for the last sixteen years, he has been making annual pilgrimages to the Madhu Shrine in August. A statement to this effect by His Lordship the Bishop of Mannar is annexed marked P1 4. Major General J. Jayasuriya USP in his letter dated 07th May 2008 to the most Reverened Dr. Rayappu JOseph, Bishop of Mannar states That we are also taking all step to secure further away from Madhu church areas and move our defence beyond 2.5 Km. so that there will be no presence of security forces personnel in the surroundings. Major General J. Jayasuriyas letter is annexed marked P2 5. The Complainant states that on 1st August 2008 he wrote to the 1st respondent regarding his intended visit to Madhu on 14th August 2008. A copy of his letter is annexed marked P3 A reminder was sent on 07th August 2008 to the 1st respondent saying that he had not received a reply to his earlier letter. A copy of the letter is annexed marked P4 6. The Complainant wrote a further letter to the 1st respondent on 12th August 2008 stating that he would be going with:- (1) The Right Reverend father Sunil de Silva, Secretary to the Archbishop of Colombo (2) Rev. Father Siri Cooray, St. Peters Branch School, Udugampola, This letter is annexed marked P5 The Complainant states that on 13th August 2008 that his Secretary received a copy of the letter from Colonel D. S. Weeraman of the Ministry of Defense, Public Security Law and Order to the Chief of Defense Staff. The 2nd paragraph of the letter stated that However this Ministry has not approved his request to stay overnight at Madhu Shrine A copy of this letter is annexed marked P6 7. The Complainant stated that at approximately 7 p. m. on 14th August 2008, while he was praying in the Church, a soldier informed him that the General who was in the Mission House wishes to speak to him. He then went to the Mission House and major General Lalith Daulagalla informed him that he had to leave at once as the Secretary, Ministry of Defence had not given him permission to stay there. He added that he (Complainant) is an Opposition Member of Parliament. He thereupon left Madhu Shrine and stayed at the Bishops House Mannar for the night and then returned to Madhu the following morning. He again spent the night of the 15th August at the Bishops House and returned to Madhu Shrine on 16th August. 8. The Complainant states that the refusal to permit him by p6 to stay the night at the Madhu Shrine and his being interrupted while he was in players is a violation of his rights set out in Article 12(1) of the Constitution namely All persons are equal before the law and are entitled to the equal protection of the law Article 12 (2) namely No Citizen shall be discriminated against on the grounds of race, religion, language, caste, sex, political opinion, place of birth or any one of such grounds and Article 14 (1) (e) namely The Freedom either by himself or in association with others and either in public or in private, to manifest his religion or belief in warship, observance, practice and teaching. 9. The Complainant states that the above violation of this fundamental rights is by executive or by administrative action. WHEREFORE the Complainant respectfully prays that your Honours Commission be pleased to : (a) conduct an immediate inquiry into this complaint. 8 - PL 002998 - (2008/06)

87 88

(b) declare the fundamental rights of the complainant. guaranteed by articles 12 (1), 12 (2) and 14 (1) (e) of the Construction have been violated.

(c) recommend to the authorities that he and other Roman Catholic pilgrims be permitted to stay at the Madhu Shrine in Order to take part in evening religious ceremonies and prayers.

(d) such other and further relief as the Commission shall deem meet.

(Sgd.) Priyalal Sirisena Attorney- at - Law

"The Island" newspaper of Monday, 8th September, 2008 states, I quote: "Sexual assault at Hakmana police station" "Police spokesman: some 'dogs' have entered service" It further states, I quote: "Police spokesman SSP Ranjith Gunasekera yesterday said that the police wouldn't shield the suspects.

He said he did not believe the police had gone to the dogs. Instead, he said, 'The dogs have come to the department'. " , ; . " " . , ? . . , , , - ( ) (Mr. Speaker) . . , [ ] .

2008 09 109 110

. . . , . , . . . , - - . . . . . , , . . . . 60 . . ; . . , , . . ; . - , - . , , . , . ( ) (Mr. Deputy Chairman of Committees) , . . . ( . . ) (The Hon. A. P. Jagath Pushpakumara) , . . . ; ; . , , , , . ? , - - ,

. , - - , , - [ ] , . . . , , . . . , . . . , . . , , . , . .

[.. 11.45 ] . ( . ) (The Hon. R. Sampanthan) Hon. Deputy Chairman of Committees, may I take this opportunity, of this Debate on the extension of the state of Emergency, to deal with a few matters of some urgent importance, relating particularly to the situation in the Vanni and I want to refer in particular to the plight of the Tamil civilians in the Vanni. Around 200,000 non-combatant Tamil civilians have been compelled to flee from their homes in view of the intense military attacks, the frequent aerial bombardment and the heavy artillery fire being engaged in by the forces of the Sri Lankan State, both by day and by night, in these areas in the Vanni. A large number of such civilians have been displaced more than once; many of them many times over and consequently, it is said that the ascertainment of the exact number of the displaced persons is difficult. Be that as it may, Sir, it is reliably estimated that around 100,000 Tamil civilians have moved into Kilinochchi in the past several days. Displacement and movement of people has also taken place in and to other areas. The intensity of the attack is unprecedented as far as Sri Lanka is concerned. Never before has such an intense attack ever occurred in this country and by international standards it is believed that the attacks presently being carried out are as bad, as the worst that have taken place at any time in any part of the world. The attacks have been ruthless and without compunction. Civilians, men, women and children have been killed,

111 112

have been grievously injured and civilian owned properties both residential and occupational and other assets belonging to civilians have been destroyed or damaged. The recklessness of the attacks, Sir, can be gauged from the fact that the Government Agent, Manner, a rank equivalent to that of a collector of a district in India and the wife of the medical superintendent of a district were injured while they were asleep in their official residences late at night in the Mannar District. The civilian population has been compelled to seek refuge in public buildings or with friends and relations and many have sought shelter in the open under trees. The UN and its related agencies and international non-governmental organizations, to the extent possible in the prevailing situation, have rendered and continue to render relief and we are grateful to these organizations for the service they are rendering to these hapless people.

The Government, though it talks big about its concern for these people, does nothing more than make available to these people the meagre food items provided under the World Food Programme. The fear, Sir, is that the worst is yet to come. It is the general expectation that the fighting will intensify in the weeks to come and in that event, it is inevitable that there will be further displacement, death and destruction. The oncoming monsoonal rains would only make the pathetic plight of these civilians even much worse. It is my duty, Sir, to place on record that what is happening to the Tamil civilians and civilian owned property in these areas in the Wanni is in violation of international human rights laws and international humanitarian laws. In order to achieve its unjust objective of militarily suppressing the legitimate political aspirations of the Tamil people, the Sri Lankan State is guilty of flagrant violations of international covenants to which it has subscribed and which, I submit, it is committed and bound to uphold. We are aware, Sir, that the UN and other international agencies are already experiencing considerable difficulties in providing relief to these people in the form of shelter, food, medicine and other essentials. Intensification in the fighting, resulting in relief workers being further hindered or in access to these areas being cut off could result in a grave humanitarian crisis of much greater proportions than what exists at present, which could result in the displaced people being denied shelter, food, medicine, drinking water and other essentials and even institutions such as hospitals ceasing to function, all of which could have calamitous consequences in relation to the Tamil civilian population, the worst affected in this dire situation being women and children. If the Sri Lankan State considers the Tamil civilian population resident in the Wanni as a segment of its own people, I submit, it is the bounden duty of the Sri Lankan

State to ensure that the Tamil civilian population in the Wanni are not compelled to experience the ordeal of such a grave humanitarian crisis. If the Sri Lankan State compels the Tamil civilian population in the Wanni to face the ordeal of such a great humanitarian crisis with serious consequences, the conclusion would be inevitable that the Sri Lankan State does not look upon these Tamil people as part of its own populace. These Tamil people have since Independence only requested the right to internal self-determination in the areas of their historical habitation. This is their most fundamental human right. The Sri Lankan State has consistently denied the Tamil people this right though democratic verdicts over several decades in the areas of their historical habitation have overwhelmingly supported this demand. The Sri Lankan State cannot deny that this is the root cause of the conflict. Even today, the Sri Lankan State is not able to place on the table a set of proposals that would satisfy the legitimate political aspirations of the Tamil people. It must be remembered that it is in this background that the Sri Lankan State today executes its current severe military operation with total unconcern for the grave consequences it causes to the Tamil civilian population. Is the Sri Lankan State, I want to ask, Sir, not unleashing on the Tamil people a programme that has genocidal connotations? Sir, I wish to next comment briefly on the situation of human rights in general in the country. People are being killed and people are going missing in all parts of the country and this is a continuing phenomenon. It happens in all the districts of the North-East and also in all other parts of the country. The Sri Lankan State is not able to bring this to an end. The Sri Lankan State is under an obligation to reveal why it cannot put an end to this situation because the question looms large as to whether, if the Sri Lankan State is not able to put an end to this situation, is it because at least some agencies or some personnel of the Sri Lankan State are a part and parcel of this agenda. Is that why the Sri Lankan State is unable to bring this situation to an end? That is a question to which there must be an answer. All efforts to establish a monitoring mechanism under the auspices of the UN have not been successful in view of the refusal of the Sri Lankan State to accept such a mechanism. I submit that such a refusal on the part of the Sri Lankan State enhances the obligation of the Sri Lankan State to bring such violations to an end. The Sri Lankan State is not able to do this either. The Sri Lankan State pleads sovereignty of the Sri Lankan State as an excuse for its refusal to accept a mechanism under UN auspices ignoring the fact that sovereignty also includes fundamental rights. Human rights and fundamental rights are inextricably intertwined and the Sri Lankan State fails to realize that when it permits the flagrant violation of human rights, it is in fact condoning the violation of Sri Lankan sovereignty and is in reality contributing to the erosion and eventual destruction of its own sovereignty.

[ . ]

2008 09 113 114

While this is the actual situation, Sir, prevalent in the country, I do not see the Sri Lankan Minister of Disaster Management and Human Rights in the House today. He seems to be going to different parts of the world and he seems, however, to be quite pleased with his performance. While this country is facing a most atrocious situation in regard to human rights, the Hon. Minister of Disaster Management and Human Rights talks as if everything is under control in this country. Sir, I want to refer to an interview that he has given, appearing in the Daily Mirror of 6th September, 2008, after he met with some UN Human Rights personnel in Geneva. And, this is what the Minister says. It states, I quote: During the working lunch, the Minister emphasized that Sri Lankas commitment to the international dialogue on promotion and protection of human rights has not been limited to its membership at the Human Rights Council and that Sri Lanka will continue to take necessary steps to improve its human rights situation. In particular, the Minister briefed the delegations on action being taken by the government to provide humanitarian assistance to the Internally Displaced Persons (IDPs),. That is all being done by the UN and by the INGOs and not by the Sri Lankan Government. .the proposed National Action Plan on Human Rights and the governments efforts to implement the voluntary pledges made at the Universal Periodic Review of Sri Lanka. The Minister welcomed the support of the international community in these endeavours. Words which, taken in their totality, mean nothing more than the expression of pious hopes and good intentions. But what is really happening on the ground? On the ground, the human rights situation is as bad as it can be. In fact, it is a matter of grave concern not merely to the people of this country, but also to various sections of the international community. Sir, let us look at what is really happening in this country. We are aware that there was a Commission of Inquiry appointed to inquire into 16 grave human rights violations. We are aware that the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons, who were appointed to be of assistance to that Commission of Inquiry and to observe that the Commission was conducting investigations in keeping with international norms and standards, has withdrawn. When they withdrew, they publicly stated that the Sri Lankan Government did not have the political or institutional will to ascertain the truth. They stated that the Sri Lankan Government was not prepared to conduct investigations into human rights violations in keeping with international norms and standards. Sir, I dealt with that matter very exhaustively in the course of the Debate on my Adjournment Motion in Parliament on the 23rd of July and I will not repeat myself. The main point that the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons made was that there was a conflict of interest by the Attorney-General participating in the proceedings before the Commission of Inquiry and leading evidence on behalf of the victims because the

Attorney-General was the legal officer of the State and was also the legal adviser to the State and was the adviser to the State in regard to various aspects of various crimes in which personnel of the Sri Lankan Government were involved. That is the main reason why the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons moved out of the process after they were satisfied that they could not play a credible role which, to themselves, was acceptable.

Even this time when the Minister went to Geneva, a representative of the Attorney-Generals Department had gone with the Minister to Geneva to defend the Sri Lankan Governments record on human rights and it is the same Department, the same Attorney-General and the same official who is said to be leading evidence on behalf of the victims before the Commission of Inquiry, clearly demonstrating the conflict of interest that prevails between his being the adviser of the Government at Geneva in defence of the Governments record on human rights and also appearing before the Commission on behalf of the victims in matters where the alleged assailants, the accused persons are personnel of the Sri Lankan Government, of the Sri Lankan State. Now, Sir, I will not deal with the IIGEP in any further detail because I want to refer to a further dimension to this whole matter which is now assuming, in my submission, grave importance. I expect the Commission of Inquiry to submit its Report by the middle of this month in regard to two investigations; one pertaining to the five university students and students who had sat for the G.C.E. (Advanced Level) Examination, who were murdered in Trincomalee in January 2006 and the other pertaining to the 17 aid-workers who were massacred in Muttur in Trincomalee in August 2006. In both these matters, it is Government personnel or armed personnel of the Sri Lankan State who are the alleged assailants or the accused. It is in regard to these two inquiries that the Commission of Inquiry is hoping to submit its Report very shortly to the President - an Interim Report or whatever. Sir, there was the Assistance and Protection to Victims of Crime and Witnesses Bill brought to this Parliament as a matter of urgency and as an urgent Bill. It was brought to Parliament on the 17th of June and then it was taken up for debate again on the 19th of June and thereafter that Bill has not been listed for further debate in this Parliament. Suddenly it has gone into a state of paralysis. I do not know why this Assistance and Protection to Victims of Crime and Witnesses Bill which was brought to Parliament as an urgent Bill, meant to be of assistance to the Commission of Inquiry in the conduct of these investigations and meant to provide protection to witnesses and victims of various crimes has suddenly gone into cold storage. I do not know why. But the question needs to be raised as to how all this has happened. As you are aware, Sir, the Commission of Inquiry recorded evidence by teleconferencing of several witnesses who had gone abroad, witnesses who are

115 116

relatives of the deceased persons or who are closely connected with the deceased persons, who had been intimidated, who were afraid to live in this country and who consequently fled this country to other countries. Their evidence could only be recorded through teleconferencing. The International Independent Group of Eminent Persons who had been giving some assistance to the Commission of Inquiry, facilitated the recording of evidence of these witnesses through teleconferencing. The Government did not provide the funds for this purpose. If the Government provided the funds there would have been no need for the Commission of Inquiry to seek funds from elsewhere. The fact of the matter was that the Government did not provide the funds. After the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons left the country, the Commission of Inquiry was handicapped and funds were not available. Certain other countries, particularly the United States, Canada and the European Union were prepared to make funds available. There would have been no need for these countries to come forward and offer to provide funds, if the Government was able to provide the funds itself which the Government did not do. The Government which claims - according to the Minister - to be interested in safeguarding human rights, in ascertaining the truth, a Government that claims to be committed not to conceal anything on which basis the Minister carries out his propaganda in various parts of the world including in Geneva. Recently in Geneva he also met with the new UN High Commissioner for Human Rights, Madam Navanethem Pillay, a former judge of the Supreme Court of South Africa, who was later a Member of the International Criminal Tribunal for Rwanda and who became even later a judge of the International Criminal Court and who presently has been appointed High Commissioner for Human Rights. Our Minister has even met her and told her that the Sri Lankan State was genuinely attempting to improve the human rights situation. But, the Government is not providing funds to the Commission of Inquiry to enable it to record by teleconferencing evidence of witnesses who can provide valuable evidence in regard to those two major crimes; the murder of five students and the murder of 17 aid-workers in Trincomalee and Mutur respectively. In this stage, when everything is in a state of abeyance, and nothing is happening about the Assistance and Protection to Victims of Crime and Witnesses Bill, some interested persons who are sponsors of a nationalist agenda in this country write to His Excellency the President and make certain representations in regard to some of the activities of the Commission of Inquiry, in regard to the recording of evidence by teleconferencing, in regard to the offer by some countries to provide funds to enable that process to continue. What does the President do? The President immediately writes to the Commission of Inquiry raising various questions, wanting various answers, issuing some - I may not call them

directions - but issuing to them certain guidelines in regard to what can be done and what cannot be done, in regard to the subject matter of inquiries. Consequently, today the resulting position is that the recording of evidence through teleconferencing has been terminated and thereby vital evidence is being kept out and is not available to the Commissioners. Assistance and Protection to Victims of Crime and Witnesses Bill brought to Parliament and debated on two days in June this year has now gone into cold storage and is not being taken up and it will die a natural death; a natural death will be pronounced before long. The Bill may not be a perfect Bill. It has several deficiencies. But the fact is that the Government is not prepared to proceed with that Bill and have that Bill passed in Parliament, of which the Government made a huge song and a dance saying that a Bill was being brought to give protection to victims and witnesses to enable them to testify without fear. The Government has put that aside and that Bill will not be taken up in Parliament. In this situation when recording of evidence by teleconferencing has been terminated or it is not being continued with, consequent to the letter from the Presidential Secretariat to the Commission of Inquiry and that the Bill itself has been put aside, the Commission of Inquiry is going to release its Interim Report to the President without such evidence being recorded. I submit, Sir, that this is a travesty of justice. This is travesty of justice. No one, other than the Commission of Inquiry has a right to determine how and through what procedure evidence will be recorded by that Commission of Inquiry. It is only that Commission of Inquiry which has the right to make that decision. That Commission of Inquiry is entitled to see, even through teleconferencing and hear the evidence of witnesses who are vital to the ascertainment of truth and the question of whether the witnesses are speaking the truth or not, whether their evidence is reliable, whether it is acceptable, whether it can be acted upon, is a matter in regard to which only the Commission of Inquiry can make any decision. It is my duty to state that it is not within the power of any one, however high in this country, based upon their own prejudices or predilections to make any effort whatever to guide the Commission of Inquiry in regard to how the Commission of Inquiry should carry out its investigations. But the fact of the matter is, Sir, that the Commission of Inquiry has been impeded, has been inhibited and stymied in the performance of its legitimate duties consequent to certain parties having an interest on behalf of the assailants and possible accused of these crimes making certain representations to the President and the Presidential Secretariat deciding thereafter - very obviously on the directions of the President - to write to the Commission of Inquiry which has resulted in this state of paralysis pertaining to the functioning of the Commission of Inquiry and probably their issuing a report shortly - as had been stated several times in the media - without the benefit of receiving the evidence of these vital witnesses even through the process of

[ . ]

2008 09 117 118

teleconferencing. Sir, this shows what importance one can attach to these statements made by, for instance, the Minister of Human Rights and other Ministers on behalf of the Government; sometimes the Foreign Minister, sometimes the Minister for Export Development and Enterprise Development and Investment Promotion and so on and so forth in different parts of the world saying that this country is committed to the ascertainment of the truth in regard to human rights violations and the Sri Lankan Government is committed to bringing an end to human rights violations. The Commission of Inquiry along with the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons was the only credible process set in motion after this Government came into being in regard to the question of human rights and initially some months ago, the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons was elbowed out. They were elbowed out; it was made impossible for them to function in this country. The Government was issuing directions, Government was passing legislation in Parliament in a manner which contradicted the advice and the position taken by the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons in regard to the conflict of interest question pertaining to the Attorney-General, and now beyond that, having elbowed out the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons the Government is effectively scuttling the Commission of Inquiry from recording all available evidence in regard to this matter and delivering a verdict or coming to a conclusion based upon all such available evidence. This clearly shows, Sir, that this Governments Agenda on the question of human rights, particularly the violation of human rights of Tamil people, as in the case of the five Tamil students and the 17 Tamil aid workers in Mutur, is a downright hoax, nothing beyond a downright hoax, that there is no sincere commitment on the part of the Government to pursue any honest investigation into the violation of human rights and the Government is staging a drama before the whole world trying to pretend that it is committed to a programme of protecting human rights in this country particularly in relation of Tamil people when there is no such commitment whatever on the part of the Government. I consider it my duty to state this on the Floor of the House because it is the Tamil people who are affected as a result of such conduct on the part of the Government and in this instance, the people affected are people from my own constituency. Now why is all this happening Sir? Before I conclude, I want to raise this question as to why all this is happening; why the Government is behaving in this way? Sir, I read an interview given recently by an Hon. Minister in the Government who is also in todays context a very important person, the Hon. Champika Ranawaka, Minister of Environment and Natural Resources and I think a close adviser of the President. I think, Sir, he spoke the truth in that recent interview and I am thankful to him because he spoke the truth. Very few people speak publicly in that way. He was asked this question. It states, I quote :

You said earlier that any call now for a political solution would affect the path of the government. Are you saying that there is no room for a political dialogue anymore? Sir, I am reading from an interview given by the Hon. Champika Ranawaka to Shakuntala Perera in the Programme Hard Talk reported in the Daily Mirror of 11th August, 2008. That was the question that the lady asked and what was the answer he gave? The answer is very, very interesting, Sir. We must put that on record. It states, I quote: This Governments path is based on a three dimensional approach towards a solution - demilitarization, democratization and development. It is the old paradigms that believed in the political solutions. This vocabulary even exists only within the NGO, INGO and embassy officials of western nations. A talk of a political solution only exists in those areas; NGOs, INGOs and embassies of western countries. I do not find my good Friend the Hon. (Prof.) Tissa Vitharana here who is talking about a political solution and the APRC process. But, this is what that Hon. Gentleman had to say. He has defined what they want to do. He further states, I quote: This will ensure that the dream of a Tamil Eelam of the TNA or the dreams of the Muslim parties will not be realized when our approach works. We never wanted Tamil Eelam. We wanted the right to internal self-determination in the areas of our historical habitation ever since the 1940s and our people have overwhelmingly supported that position at democratic verdicts over several decades, not at one election but several elections over several decades. We were compelled to demand Tamil Eelam because you were not conceding or accepting the right to internal self-determination in our areas of historical habitation. Now, you have brought the Muslims also along with us, our Tamil-speaking brethren who live with us in the North-East and who today are the victims of your nationalistic agendas as much as we are victims. We are grateful to you for that also. What does he go further and say, Sir? The most significant part of his answer is, I quote: The Sinhala nationalist movement has finally taken the reigns; the others will simply have to fall in line. Finally this government is not under any pressure to sacrifice the rights of the Sinhala people. We are not wanting the rights of the Sinhala people to be sacrificed, certainly not. We want the rights of the Sinhala people to be recognized and we want this Government to fulfil the rights of the Sinhala people. But, we also ask that the rights of the Tamil-speaking people in this country be also fulfilled, that we be allowed to live in this country with dignity and self-respect. This is the Sinhala nationalist agenda which has been the cause of the scuttling of the Commission of Inquiry, the elbowing out of the International Independent Group of Eminent Persons and today is scuttling the work

119 120

of the Commission of Inquiry where they cannot even record evidence to be able to ascertain the truth in regard to what happened. This is the agenda, Sir, that is at work. So, what is the position of the Government today? Are you for a Sri Lankan identity? Are you for a Sri Lankan agenda or, is it your belief as very, very clearly enunciated by a very important Minister in your Government, a person whom I consider as being a more important Minister than many other Ministers in this Government, that your agenda is Sinhala nationalism, a Sinhala country, a Sinhala Sri Lanka where the others will have to just fall in line, they have no say? I want to say, Sir, that that cannot happen. We are certainly prepared to be a part and parcel of a Sri Lankan identity based upon our dignity and self-respect and as equal citizens in this country. We are certainly prepared to contribute to a Sri Lankan cultural mosaic, but if anyone thinks that we can be compelled to fall in line and be slaves within a Sinhala identity and within the contours of Sinhala nationalism I think, such people are making a grave mistake. And let all these Ministers who go abroad and who even in this country try to project that the Government is pursuing a different agenda please realize that you are not speaking the truth when you say that. The Governments true agenda is the agenda which has been very clearly enunciated by the Minister, the Hon. Patali Champika Ranawaka in his interview to the Daily Mirror. I say, Sir, this must stop. I raised this matter of the Commission of Inquiry because two grave crimes which the Government pretended to inquire into with a measure of honesty today are being sidelined. The Commission of Inquiry is not being allowed to perform its functions. I am not making any allegation against the Commission of Inquiry. There are persons on that Commission of Inquiry whom I hold in the highest respect. They are persons of great rectitude and independence but the fact of the matter is that they are not being allowed to perform their duties as they would very much want to. I, therefore state, Sir, that this Government is today by the prosecution of this war in the Vanni and by its general failure to observe human rights in all parts of the country really wanting to fulfil the Sinhala nationalist agenda which has been so very clearly articulated by the Hon. Patali Champika Ranawaka, Minister of Environment and Natural Resources. Thank you, Sir.

Subscription : The annual subscription for Official Report of Hansard is Rs. 2,178. A single copy of Hansard is available for Rs. 18.15. (Postage Rs. 2.50) Copies can be obtained by remitting in advance an annual subscription fee to the SUPERINTENDENT, GOVERNMENT PUBLICATION BUREAU, No. 132, Maya Avenue, Kirulapone, Colombo 5. The fee should reach him on or before November 30 each year . Late application for subscriptions will not be accepted.
